Cassia Garden Circle for Jewish Ladies
Organized in 1960, Cassia Garden Circle, an affiliate of the Garden Club of Jacksonville, is a
group of Jewish women who are interested in gardening. Many of the charter members are still
active in the group.
Cassia is a group of tropical trees, shrubs and plants with compound leaves, yellow flowers and
long pods, found in Israel. The Garden Club meets monthly. Programs have included Japanese
Flower Arranging, bonsai, hanging baskets, underwater arrangements and potpourri. Many
exciting plans have been made for next year’s programming. Spend an interesting morning, and
enjoy a light lunch with some pleasant ladies. If you are interested call Jean Goodman at 733-1565.

The Progressive Credit Union was begun in 1940 to provide a measure of financial service to persons of the Jewish faith in
Jacksonville.
Consumer loans are made to members for family, personal and business needs. New ideas are constantly being explored to
assist in the financial needs.
Belonging to the Credit Union is an excellent form of savings. The safety of savings is fully protected at all times. All
members receive free Life Insurance on their savings, up to $2,000.00. All loans are covered with free Credit Life Insurance for
the full outstanding balances. The interest rate charged is lower than the interest rate of most lending institutions in the
Jacksonville area. All savings are insured up to $100,000 by the Florida Credit Union Guarantee Corporation.
The Progressive Credit Union is supervised by the Board of Directors who are elected by the membership. All officers are
directors of this community project serve without compensation whatsoever.
We extend a cordial invitation for all to join in the Progressive Credit Union to build a stronger Jewish Community in
Jacksonville. For information please call the Progressive Credit Union Office. 354-4770.

volunteers at the Art Museum to bring and discuss art in the
public and private schools. Our Mental Health Forum, co¬
sponsored with the Mental Health Association and Florida
Junior College, attracted over 2,000 participants.
Our newest project, CASA (Court Appointed Special
Advocates), trains volunteers to act as a “friend of the
court” in the best interest of an abused or neglected child. A
CASA is a guardian ad litem in accordance with Florida law.
Each CASA attends two training sessions, three hours
each, conducted by professionals in the field. In addition,
on-going education programs will be offered by the staff,
and legal counsel will be available to provide advice and
assistance, and, if necessary, to appear in court with the
CASA. For further information and application forms, call
the program office, 633-3709.

The National Council of Jewish Women is a volunteer
organization dedicated in the spirit of Judaism to advancing
human welfare and the democratic way of life. Through a
coordinated program of education, service, advocacy and
social action, NCJW works in the Jewish and general
communities, locally, nationally and internationally.
Our local projects include: Preschool vision testing to
discover sight problems, service to the foreign born, Art
Enrichment Program (“Picture Lady”) which trains
NCJW’s commitment to Israel dates back to the years
before there was an Israel, to the years when Jews around
the world were working hand in hand to establish a Jewish
state.
Within Israel NCJW’s strong programs in education and
social welfare have helped to develop the country’s lead¬
ership.
For membership information, please contact any of our
officers.

ORT in Jacksonville
To my sister Jewess,
Women’s American ORT is the most complex, exciting, dynamic
and fastest growing Jewish women’s organization in the U.S. We are an
activist group not only taking stands, but positively working to upgrade
the quality of life for ourselves, our families and our communities.
We are very involved in public education as well as career and
vocation education. Not only have we our first school (highly
acclaimed) in New York and a second school about to open in Los
Angeles, but we are most excited about the new Jewish High School in
North Miami where ORT has been asked not only to run the science and technological tracts, but also to help create the total
curriculum!
Not only have we 800 installations of various types of schools in 24 countries on five continents with two million student
graduates in our 102 year history; not only are we known as the finest vocational educators in the world; not only does our
government recognize our expertise, call on our testimony before congressional committees and have ORT members on
educational governmental boards on every echelon of government but we are . . . take stands . . . and act to uphold the right of
abortion, fight for passage of the ERA, work for human rights and freedom of movement for all peoples, especially Soviet Jewry
and support Israel Americans and Jews (half of our ORT network of schools are there.) We confront this new radical right
movement head on, fighting against censorship, prayer in schools, right to life through anti-democratic and anti-pluralistic views.
Most importantly, we have assumed a vanguard role to thwart anti-Semitism wherever it raises its ugly head.
This, very briefly, is our program. Our chapters are as pluralistic as our country. Their diversity creates the right place for you
to have your voice heard on the most momentous issues of our harried times and our 600 members in Jacksonville and 145,000 in
the U.S. help give you strength to make your voice heard - loud and clear!
Won’t you make Women’s American ORT stronger? Can you afford in all conscience not to belong?
ORTistically, Sandy Miller

WE GET TO GO ON THE MOUNTAIN, MOSES.
We have been traveling in the valley
Only to rest and pray to “Father”
We start out as a “lost stranger”
But we continue along our path of life
God praises us and says “Hallelujah”
With everlasting joy to lighten our hearts.
Mother, cry not for the child of the future
The light of God will protect us forever,
We grow as the flowering tree
Our joys will make us sing and dance
Just look at the sky above it never changes
Faith, God and Love will never die.
Our Treasure will never fail us
Our Sefer Torah is the light.
Our new Generation is our Treasure and will
Never be lost
Your real contribution is not money
But your Love of God is what is important.
Amen.

Jewish War Veterans
LT. MEYER LIEBOVITZ POST 199
Jacksonville, Florida
■ JWV is more than a veterans organiza¬
tion. More than a Jewish organization. It is
an amalgamation of Americans of Jewish
faith who share the common experience of
having served their country in time of war.
■ JWV was founded in 1896 to counteract
slurs against Jewish patriotism. Since then,
it has been in the forefront of the battle
against anti-Semitism, bigotry and preju¬
dice. In upholding American democratic
traditions, JWV fights injustice and discrim¬
ination of all kinds.
■ JWV contributes greatly to the growth of
a sympathetic understanding of Israel and
its problems among all Americans. It is out¬
spoken on issues that are affecting per¬
manent peace in the Middle East. Likewise,
its leadership role continues to help arouse
American public opinion against Soviet
Union’s anti-Jewish policies.
■ JlW’s views are well known to Congress
on such diverse subjects as foreign policy,
civil rights, defense spending, veterans
benefits, housing and education.
■ JWV, through its hospital, rehabilitation
and veterans service programs, assists the
veteran and his dependents in many ways.
It maintains veteran service offices, manned
by professional experts, in major cities
throughout the country.
■ JWV, through its child welfare program,
supports the Boy Scout organization, pro¬
vides summer camp scholarships for under¬
privileged children, sponsors athletic league
tournaments. Its program includes sponsor¬
ship of brotherhood rallies and the under¬
taking of civic betterment projects in local
communities.

Nathan Friedlin
The State of Israel honored Nathan Freidlin at
an Israel Bond Breakfast on November 16,1981.
Mr. Freidlin was chosen to receive the “Lion of
Judah Award” because his life best exemplifies
the highest tradition of service to his synagogue,
community and to the state of Israel.
A lifelong resident of Jacksonville, Mr.
Friedlin has been a member of the Board of the
Center for over 30 years and is a past president.
He has also served on the Religious committee
for over 20 years. He is a familiar face to all those
who attend Shabbat Services. A visitor of Israel
four times, Mr. Freidlin recalls one of the most
memorable times when he visited Israel in 1976
with the Chumash Study Group.
Nathan is married to his lovely wife, Ann.
They have two sons, Mel and A1 and two grand¬
children. We wish the family mazeltov.
...stop by and visit Regency Flouse, Jacksonville’s
Retirement Address of Distinction. We think you’ll
like what you see.
We offer continuing life-care for people who have
worked hard for secure, comfortable, independent,
worry-free retirement living.
If you can’t stop by, write or call for our brochure.
Jacksonville Regency House
33 West Adams Street, Jacksonville, FI. 32202 (904) 358-1832
Operated by Presbyterian Homes of the Synod of Florida

===== PAGE 270 =====
Passover for All Project
Ricky Plotkin and Steven Shapiro are busy calling for sponsors.
“Let all who are hungry come to eat.” The youth of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center undertook a most meaningful project to make those words a reality.
Each student in each of the schools and youth groups was requested to bring a
minimum of .50 to be used to purchase food for needy Jewish families for
Passover.
Another part of this project was the sponsorship of those individuals who had
no seder to attend. Our young people were responsible for calling the entire
congregation and asking for their support and help in this effort. The response
was most gratifying. Over 20 boxes of Passover foods were distributed.
Karen Manasse, Miriam Mibab, Stacy
Ginsburg and Manya Lazarus display some of
the foods that were included in the Passover
boxes.
Youth and Education Banquet
Horty Gendzier explains the Ramah program, Mistress of Ceremonies,
Marsha Pollock listens.
At this annual banquet the Center extends it appreciation to
students, teachers and staff for all their hours of work and
effort on its behalf.
The new boards of USY and Kadima were installed. The
highlight of the evening was the showing of “The World of Our
Grandparents,” a special video tape that was filmed during
that fabulous weekend.
Todd Berman recites the Hamotzi
Rabbi Gaffney presents Rabbi Kentof with a surprise ... an original oil painting
of Rabbi Kentof painted by Blanche Slott.

The State of Israel presents
The Medilerraiieaii - Dead Sea Canal Project
Israel announces its most ambitious economic project; the building of a Canal from the
Mediterranean to the Dead Sea for production of Hydro-Electric power.
The Canal will ultimately produce more than 20% of Israel’s total Energy needs and alleviate
to a larger extent the import of oil which in 1980 cost 25 billion dollars.
As water cascades from the High ground on the Mediterranean to the Dead Sea the Canal will
provide Hydro-Electric power which by the year 2000 should produce 3,000 megawatts of
electricity out of a national total of 10,000 megawatts.
The Canal will provide solar ponds to soak up heat from the sun, make water available for
cooling future power stations.
The Canal will also create lakes for tourist attractions, agricultural projects and fisheries and
establish industrial and building enterprises.
The Canal project lifts the importance of Israel Bonds to a higher than ever level. While more
than 5 billion dollars in Israel Bonds has been sold world Jewry will quickly produce another
billion dollars to provide the funds for this historic project.
You can be part of that history.
The State of Israel Bond organization is the exclusive group, responsible for the raising of
$100 Million in 1981-82 as seed money for this project.
For additional information contact Dr. Nelson Goldman, Jacksonville chairman, or write Mr. Bert
Sales, State of Israel Bonds, Box 667, Palm Beach, Fla 33480.
